Oh you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the end of the knowledge of medicine along with its contents, and I have finished it through its explanations and by its declarations. And it came to me in vision that I would complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is completely unknown everywhere, so the science has perished and been lost, and nothing remains from it except the small descriptions in books by the ancients that hands have moved. And because of this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed off and true knowledge is estranged.
It seems to me that I will make it live together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation. and I will come together with the forms of cautery instruments and other tools of the work along with the adjustment of their declaration and preparation as it is necessary.
And because there are no good masters of hands in our time, the art of medicine has been estranged. And it is necessary for someone who undertakes this to ascend to the science of anatomy, as Galien says, so long as he knows the justice of members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and the number of them, and their arrangement and moving and resting veins, and from where their origin is.
And therefore says Hippocrates that a name is much if it has a name, and with the work it is little. and all the more so in the art of surgery.
We tell you in the introduction to this book that whoever is not aware of the things previously said should beware lest they err and injure men.
in such a way that I have often seen many of those who meddle with this science and abandon their own knowledge and experience.
I saw a foolish surgeon who cut out an abscess from the neck of a woman, and cut into her arteries. for which so much blood came out that the woman fell dead between his hands.
And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone from a man's bladder, and the stone was large; so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man inside died in three days.
And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the state of the sick person and the size of the ulcer, and I knew that if they were to cut it out, he would die.
And I saw another surgeon who took care of a duke of our land who had his leg broken and with the breakage was wounded;
and the surgeon, full of ignorance, bound the break above the wound with tight stitches and did not let the wound have any dressing at all, and thus left it to its end;
and he commanded that he not untie it.
and remains so until the leg is completely bloated and swelled, and comes to destruction.
I am called to come to him, and I hurry to come to loosen the leg; and when I had loosened it so, it was set at ease and did not feel any pain.
But all the corruption of the member was already confirmed, and I could not heal it;
and the corruption did not cease to go through the member until the entire member was completely lost.
And I saw another physician who drained a suppurating abscess, and then inflamed it further through the wickedness of his treatment.
For an ulcer, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it does not seem fitting that one touch it with iron unless it is in such a place where one can entirely remove what is corrupted.
And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: that is to say, work in which there is danger in many situations;
and I will show you in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Why it is necessary to keep yourself informed, so that foolish men may not speak badly of you.
If you take your arms in custody, and treat your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through the grace of God you may come to salvation and be praised;
and leave the frightful diseases to severe treatment;
and take your arms from what causes you to doubt, and have courage in yourself so that you may come into this world to the other of glory.
Galien says in some of his warnings: Do not undertake a sick person that you are called a foolish doctor.
I have written this treatise according to three chapters.
The first chapters are of fire cauterizations and of hot medicinal cauterizations, and the chapter is ordered from head to feet;
and of the forms of instruments, and of the cauterizing irons, and of all that is necessary in the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and venesections and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things.
and it contains the chapters ordered and the forms of instruments.
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things.
and it contains the chapters ordered from head to foot, and the forms of instruments.
So that we remember the work, it is necessary for me to tell the quality of the help and the harm of each temperament.
I say that the quality of healing and its harm is the longest and most subtle speech and the secret responses.
and many wise people spoke of this and agreed with it;
and they shortened their words because I drew out the length.
I say that the fire cautery helps universally to all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions. that is to say hot complexion with matter, and dry complexion with matter.
In a hot and dry complexion together with matter, no one disagreed and said that cautery there is a great aid; and the others said the opposite: that cautery is of no value for diseases that come from heat and dryness. For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure a hot disease with heat or dryness.
and he who said the opposite says that cautery makes great aid for hot and dry diseases that come into the body of men. For when you compare the body of man to its moisture in the constitution of fire, you find the body cold.
And I agree with this statement. For I have found it to be true at times through experience.
And in any case, do not interfere with it unless you are a doctor who has tried it, and who knows through long experience the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the cures and the timing of the time.
we are not at all afraid of other conditions, especially in cold and damp illnesses. And all the doctors gathered together and agreed on cauterizing.
And know, son, that cauterizing with fire is a secret of the cure, and of greater goodness than cauterizing with burning medicine.
For fire is simple, and it does not harm except the member that is burned, and it does not hurt another member if you know its name.
The hot medicines come from member to another by dislocating, and bring great sickness of difficult healing to the affected member. and it is likely that the patient will die.
The fire because of its height and the goodness of its substance does not do this, if there is no excessiveness.
And I have found this by experimentation and the great length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it was established on the truth of things.
and for this reason I excuse myself for the length of the discourse, because it does not please me that I take away from you the secret which is revealed by fire and the quality of the work, how it drives out diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating. You receive it in your thoughts.
And know, son, that they agreed on what time the cauterizations should be done, and appointed assistants.
And I say that cautery is advisable at all times, because the hurtful things beneath are put right with the help of the cautery. and in the same way if the cauterizations are for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait for the time when greater mischief comes to the member.
And never think, dear son, as foolish people do; for the illness that is cured by cauterization does not have a return. and they say so.
and they say so. but it is not as they think, because cauterization is not just a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors that are cause of the pain, and is worth more than other medicines for its haste, and the virtue of its work and its power.
And a possible thing is that the disease comes at some time according to the temperament of the patient and the location of the disease and its nature.
and the excesses are gathered in him by acquiring meat and similar things; if there aren't cauterizing administered to the place where there is a lot of excess and moisture, as with fire cauterization for pain, and similar things, and this pain does not come back. but it happens often.
And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and that's true.
but they do not believe that cauterization is worth after medicine, but their intention is false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer ways of treatment in any disease and they are not worth it, then we administer cauterization, and it works.
Therefore it is clearly seen that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
The old ones said that cauteries made with instruments of gold are more deadly than those made with iron; and they do not say this only because of the quality of gold and its high substance.
and they said that the place of the cautery does not become infected, but it is not true for I have tested it and found that it is true in certain men;
and gold cauteries are worth more than iron ones, as they said. And nonetheless when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it quickly cools down;
and if one heats it too much; they are reduced to ash. and thus there is enough hindrance.
Now I have ordered this chapter from the head to the foot so that the view is easier to find.
These cauteries are used for moist and cold on the brain, and there are two which are done because of an illness called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the head towards themselves, and towards the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and similarly to all illnesses that come from coldness such as paralysis and dropsy and apoplexy and similar illnesses.

And they said the old ones that when a wound is left open longer, it becomes purer. and on this account, we aid it with movement.
And one of them said that the cautery should be left in place until part of the bone is charred, and then remove what has been burned off from the bone, and treat it.
And they say the other that one must let it cool on a cautery so long, and press so hard that you lower from the bone as wide as the thread that women put in their purses so that the humors may flow out.
and one must leave the wound open for a long time. after that one must cure and sew it up.
And these two manners of cauterizing do not seem to me in any way good at all, except that in some men there is a means of fear.
And it seems to me that I must leave it.
for the shoulder is weakened by continuous flow of nature, as we witness in other members;

the eyelash which points the eye At times the hairs around the eyelids become converted to stingers, and prick the eye, and it is done with a cauterization according to two methods: that is to say of fire, or of burning medicine.

Of the treatment of a fistula by cauterization
When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you make it cauterize in this manner.
Instruct the patient to put his head in your armpit; and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor leave his head.
then put moistened cotton in an egg white or in pomegranate juice on the eye;
after that heat the cautery which is similar:
and hold it to his head as a shape of a goose feather, together with the quill being the cautery;
If you look, it is pricked from one end to the other, and if you look, it is also like a tent;
But nonetheless, that which is prickled is moved for your work.
Afterwards press the fistula so it is open, and remove the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, then work on it, and drain outside the bowels;
Afterwards put on the hot cauterizing iron, and hold your hand to the cauter on the part below the eyelid, so that your hands do not go mad; and place the cauter in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
If you come to the beginning of the cauterization just up to the bone, it would be good. If not, then start again with the cauter once more, or if you need to, and leave it for three days;
After I put on moist cotton in a ball, and the treatment of ointment drying out so that they are healed, and if forty days have passed without being healed, then put on caustic medicine until the bone is exposed. and the king according to what he would come in his chapter.

of toothache or dental pain
When the toothache comes from cold, whether from hot or cold things, and medicines do not help, then there is need of cauterizing in two ways: and a caustic made from wax and a fire cauterization.
A caustic of wax is such that you take beeswax, and the end in a spoon made of iron or lead; after take some cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent needle, and moisten in boiling wax, and put it on the aching tooth quickly and hold until it cools.
and so do this often until the virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the linen and cotton are moist in cold wax, and put it on the aching tooth, and put on the hot iron until the fire comes to the gum of the tooth.

after heating the cautery, its shape will come out like this afterwards, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down.

the cure for chancre by cauterization
When a cancer comes at the beginning, and you see it arresting, then cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the edge of the cancer.

and it seems to me that this is not good anyway, for I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen once.
and a more direct thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizations.

We have already said in the section on the treatment of wounds;
We will tell you the treatments of hands and of medicine, according to completion.
I say that wounds are diverse in accordance with how they were made, and in accordance with the place or location where the wound was made, and what they were made by.
The things by which wounds are made are by falling of stone, and cutting with sword and knife or spear or lance or club or arrow or similar things.
or are made according to the places of the body, as a wound that strikes on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members.
and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, for the memory comes in its chapter.
I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from falling of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is great, and you doubt lightly of hot abscess. If it heals quickly from the head itself even if there is bleeding from the wound, and the healing takes place on the opposite side of the damaged part;
and instruct the patient to abstain from wine and thick meats.
And if it does not heal, then let the patient eat thin meat, and not drink wine, nor chew cooked flesh;
and put on the wound a poultice with charred onions in rose oil alone, or in vinegar.
and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh and full of blood, and not changed by the air, powder that I will name later;
and if the sore has been changed to a boil, then put on some salves until it is healed.
And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the edges cannot be closed by stitching, then close them with sutures, just as I will say about the belly wounds, in the chapter on suture.
If the wound is discovered to be of the bone, and it can penetrate, and only holds by a small thread, so cut it. Then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meat, such as roasted head and boiled bread, as well as chickens, and similar things.
And if you find corruption in the skin, but it has not reached the bone, so cut out all the corruption and pour away pus, then treat it.
and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped by medicines, so cut the artery, and if you find it severed, then tie it with a thread. and if this does not help, then burn it.
And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy. And you put this powder on, which heals it, after the iron has moved it.
And the manner of making this powder is: take incense a part; the blood of a dragon two parts; heat up the live calcined [material] three parts, and mix it finely, and apply the wound, and bind it firmly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood again;
and then tie it tightly, and let it be without untying, if it does not swell; for you do not remove the medicine until it is healed.
And at times one makes this mixture of calamine alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but the wound has become festering and inflamed.
And if the iron has moved the wound, or made a hole in it, do not put this powder on it at all;
but apply some digested ointments, or poultices made with barley flour and water and honey, until it discharges pus; then the doctor treats other wounds until they are healed.
And if a bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, then extract with fine pincers;

of intestinal rupture.
The ruptures of the belly are great and middle-sized and small;

because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, they set in better with pins, and because of this it is more advantageous to sew the middle wound, therefore one sews the intestine back into place before the other two.

When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the belly, it behooves you to make the patient lie on his back, and set his legs higher than his head. and if it is in the part below the belly, so set the head and pelvis higher than the parts below, and also the curvature of the belly will be in one of the two parts so that the injured part will be higher than the other;

In small wounds place the dressing that is attached to you, then take between your hands the minister's patty which covers the entire curvature at his hand, and put together the lips;
and this is the common manner of stitching, and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound a double thickness, and stick in a needle where there is good thread strong; and pierce the two keys of the skin with the two keys of the leather, which is beneath the skin inside, as far as you make it pierce from that part, and put together the two heads of the leather the four parts;
Then tie with a doubled thread around the needle of two parts, then join together the two bones of the wound properly, and then let them be for two days' space, and insert another needle;
Then tie the thread double as you have done for the first needle, and cease not to do this with the needles, so long as all of the wound is restrained;
and let the needles be of medium size between fine and thick, for the fine needles pierce all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot well enter; therefore it is necessary that they be medium-sized;
and it does not seem good to thrust the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and open up the wound in front of the suturing;
and then remove the points of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and put tents or a cloth over the points of the needles to keep them steady, and let them be until the wound is sutured;
and this manner of stitching with needles is more advisable for small wounds, because it suffices with one needle or two.
The second stitch is common, and it consists of assembling the two pieces of leather and the two pieces of skin together with one needle where there is a strong thread in the middle.
and when you have pierced these pieces together, then draw out the needle at the part where you began, in the manner that one sews cloth.
and put a thread of the thickness of a small thimble between each stitch.
this stitch is known to men, and I sewed a wound that a man had on his belly, which was hurt by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm in width, and the intestines were well exposed two palms in width, and the wound was within the belly.
I brought him back his intestines after he had been without them for 24 hours and the wound was sown up just to 15 days, and he cured it, and was healed.
And the physician had judged that he was going to die, and it was a miracle;
and did not cure him with ointment, for I was in such a place where one could not find any, nor any medicine; and placed some old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed him with honey water until he was healed.
Now I will tell you two proper ways of stitching:
take the needle, and push it through from the outer part just to the inner part;
when it has pierced through right to right, then bring the end of the thread or cord that you have passed the needle through, and make it pierce from the inner part just to the outer part;
and the understanding of this stitching is that you stitch in such a way as clothiers make felt, and that you leave one end of the thread once, and take it up again on the other side, until the stitching is completely done.
The second manner of sewing, which the Greeks call properly, is so that some do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the silk to the other end.
stitch a needle or end of the thread nearby, and make a small hole in that place alone, and leave the two ends of the silk; then turn the needle, and make a hole through from the outside part just up to the inside part, with the two ends of the silk.
then make a hole in one and the other from the outside part just up to the inside part, through two other eyes of the thread that are on the opposite side.
and this is the mother manner of sewing and the most common.
The Greeks say this phrase, and some bear witness to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, or have thread in each.
One must stick one needle here, and the other there, in the manner of those who sew corsets.
and you should know that when a rupture is inside the belly, the suturing is more grievous than in other places of the belly.

And now it is fitting that I make you aware of the treatment of fistula which is done by handwork.

and I will tell you of an ulcer that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take it as an example and aid in your work.
He was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came inside the body, so much so that materials came to the leg and he was swelling with a large abscess, and he did not have any reason outside for it to be opened.

worms that are born between skin and flesh This disease is called in our land "disease of the ox" because it often occurs with cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes all over the body rising and descending, and causes pain to move from member to member, until it bursts the skin where it goes, and discharges.
and is a sign of corruption of some humour, such as comes with worms and serpents and lice and ascarids from the belly;

from the pain that comes from windiness This disease is called "vakirir" in our land; it is a pain that occurs in certain members, and can move from member to member.
and I have seen what I am telling you. I was called to an ailing woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the middle of her upper arm.
and I saw it spread after that, up to the shoulder, just as quickly as a worm spreads out, or like bright silver when it moves from place to another.
the pain moved away from that place and settled in the shoulder, and then a little after it ran through the whole body, so that it came to the other arm.

and they did not appear in those who are well-nourished, and who have moist bodies and responding veins.

Splinters are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
The diversities of them are that there are those with great points, small ones, hairy ones, and blunt ones; and of those with two angles, and of those with wings, and of those with pieces.
and that which slips into any member so it slips in two manners: or into the principal member that drops, such as brain, heart, liver, womb, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members. When it slips then in any place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you afterwards becomes apparent: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for many die afterwards in various conditions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces it and perforates the bone, and shoots out the splinter which is above the brain, is when there is scotoma and swoon and vomiting and vertigo in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of gall. and perchance it will burst from the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps speech and voice are lost. and there is an effusion of white moist discharge from the wound, resembling pus, and also it jumps like a boil on flesh.
and if you notice these signs, then hold back from the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
The signs of the arrowhead when it penetrates into the heart are that it is close to the left breastbone, and feels as though it was stuck in a hard, not empty thing. and perhaps the arrowhead becomes putrid like pus, and there is black bloody discharge, and comes forth cold sweat, and fainting. therefore know without doubt that death approaches.
And the sign of the splinter when it lodges in the liver is that bloody foam bursts out from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the sick person changes color, and gasps for breath and seeks cold air.
And if the arrowhead falls into the covering of the liver, it is near to the small ribs; And throws a great anguish and great pain and sighs; and moves all the limbs of the shoulders.
And if the splinter lodges in the stomach, perhaps something that is undigested meat comes out from the wound.
And if the splinter lodges in the belly and comes out through the intestine without any signs of digestion, then there is no hope for a cure or for extracting the splinter.
And if an arrowhead pierces the bladder and the urine bursts out and comes forth, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is mortal.
The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and forearms and calves and legs and similar parts, are safe according to various conditions. Of veins from which one becomes well are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen at the head, namely: two vessels that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech". and the two arteries that are in the two visible temples; and two veins that are in the two corners of the two eyes, which are called "aspires". and the vein that is in the forehead; and the veins that are at the back of the neck. and the two tendons that are in the neck. and the two veins that are above the lips of the mouth, and they are called "augeherich". and two veins that are under the tongue.
The veins which one commonly drains are like a "V" in each arm.
one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head". and the median one is called "facia", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the common people call it "vein of the heart". and the basilic vein is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the elbow, and it is that one which drains, which opens obviously above the armpit.
And the saphena vein is the vein which is between the ring and middle fingers, and it has two branches.

The book of wounds begins here. (Note: this likely marks the end of the section on ventouses and the beginning of a new chapter in the medical text) This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a treatment for wounds and swellings.
